25:T3848,<entryFree id="n5586" key="جَرَمَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">جَرَمَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">جرم</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">جرمه</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">جرمة</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">جَرِمَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">جَرْمٌ</foreign>, (S,) [like <foreign lang="ar">جَزَمَهُ</foreign>,] <hi rend="ital">He cut it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cut it off.</hi> (S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّاةَ</foreign>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ صُوفَ الشَّاةِ</foreign>, (S,) inf. n. as above, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">He shore,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sheared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cut off the wool of, the sheep.</hi> (S, K, * TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمْتُ مِنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I took</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">clipped somewhat</hi>] <hi rend="ital">from it;</hi> [namely, the wool;] like <foreign lang="ar">جَلَمْتُ</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ النَّخْلَ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) aor. as above, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">جَرْمٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">جَرَامٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">جِرَامٌ</foreign>, (S, * K,) <hi rend="ital">He cut the palmtrees;</hi> (Msb;) [meaning] <hi rend="ital">he cut off the fruit of the palm-trees;</hi> (S, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n5586-1" target="اجترمهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (S:) and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ التَّمْرَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">he cut off the dates.</hi> (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا زَمَنُ الجَرَامِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الجِرَامِ</foreign>, (S,) i. e. [<hi rend="ital">This is</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the time of the cutting off of the fruit of the palm-trees.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ النَّخْلَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">جَرْمٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He computed by conjecture the quantity of fruit upon the palm-trees;</hi> (K;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n5586-2" target="اجترمهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (Lh, K:) [like <foreign lang="ar">جَزَمَهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اجتزمهُ</foreign>.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ</foreign>, (S, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">جَرِمَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">جَرْمٌ</foreign>, (TK,) also signifies <hi rend="ital">He gained, acquired,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">earned,</hi> [wealth, &amp;c.,] (S, K,) <foreign lang="ar">لِأَهْلِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">for his family;</hi> and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n5586-3" target="اجترم" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (K.) And you say, <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ يَجْرِمُ لِأَهْلِهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَجْرِمُ أَهْلَهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He went forth seeking</hi> [sustenance], <hi rend="ital">and practising skill,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">artifice, for his family.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَجْرِمَنَّكُمْ شَنَآنُ قَوْمٍ</foreign>, in the Kur [v. 3 and 11], is explained by some as meaning <hi rend="ital">And let not a people's hatred by any means occasion you.</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cause you:</hi> or it means <hi rend="ital">let not a people's hatred by any means induce you,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">incite you.</hi> (S, TA.) Some read   
      <foreign lang="ar">لا <ref cref="n5586-4" target="يُجْرِمَنَّكُمْ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, with damm to the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>; and Zj says that <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمْتُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَجْرَمْتُ</foreign> signify the same: but some say that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">let it not by any means lead you into crime,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sin;</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَجْرَمْتُهُ</foreign> being like <foreign lang="ar">آثَمْتُهُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">I led him into sin,</hi> &amp;c. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Fr says that the asserting <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمْتُ</foreign> to mean <foreign lang="ar">حَقَقْتُ</foreign> [or rather <foreign lang="ar">حُقِقْتُ</foreign>, for this is evidently, I think, the right reading, though I find <foreign lang="ar">حَقَقْتُ</foreign> in the TA as well as in a copy of the S, in another copy of which I find <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَتْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حَقَّقَتْ</foreign>, suggesting that the right reading may perhaps be <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَتْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حُقَّتْ</foreign>,] is nought: they who so explain it having been confused in their judgment by the saying of the poet Aboo-Asmà, (S, TA,) or, as some say, El-Howfazán, (TA,) or, accord. to some, 'Ateeyeh Ibn-'Ofeyf, (IB, TA,) <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَلَقَدْ طَعَنْتُ أَبَا عُيَيْنَةَ طَعْنَةً</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَتْ فَزَارَةَ بَعْدَهَا أَنْ يَغْضَبُوا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> in which they made <foreign lang="ar">فزارة</foreign> to be in the nom. case, as though the meaning were <foreign lang="ar">حُقَّ لَهَا الغَضَبُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">it was right,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fit,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">proper, for it,</hi> (the tribe of Fezárah,) <hi rend="ital">to be angry;</hi> nearly agreeing with an explanation of <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ</foreign> given by Golius as on the authority of Ibn-Maaroof, namely, “ meritus, dignus fuit ”]: but, he says, <foreign lang="ar">فزارة</foreign> is in the accus. case; the meaning being, <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَتْهُمُ الطَّعْنَةُ أَنْ يَغْضَبُوا</foreign> [which will be found explained, on the authority of IB, in what follows]: AO says that the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">أَحَقَّتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الغَضَبَ</foreign>, i. e., <foreign lang="ar">أَحَقَّتِ الطَّعْنَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَزَارَةَ أَنْ يَغْضَبُوا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">حَقَّت</foreign> also, [both having the same signification, i. e., <hi rend="ital">the thrust required Fezá- rah to be angry,</hi>] from <foreign lang="ar">لَا جَرَمَ لَأَفْعَلَنَّ كَذَا</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">حَقًّا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily I will do thus</hi>]: (S, TA:) accord. to Fr, the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">كَسَبَتْ فَزَارَةَ الغَضَبَ عَلَيْكَ</foreign>, the right reading being, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَقَدْ طَعَنْتَ</foreign>, with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>; [so that the verse means <hi rend="ital">And verily thou didst thrust Aboo-'Oyeyneh with a thrust</hi> of thy spear <hi rend="ital">that occasioned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused, Fezárah, after it, to be angry</hi> against thee:] for he is addressing Kurz El-'Okeylee, bewailing his death; and Kurz had thrust Aboo-'Oyeyneh, who was Hisn Ibn-Hudheyfeh Ibn-Bedr El-Fezáree. (IB, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">جَرَمَ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">جَرِمَ</orth>
